<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Three Months 
Ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 Compared to the Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009</I></B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Net Sales. </I>Net sales consist primarily
of gross sales of gasoline and diesel fuel net of
excise taxes, general merchandise, and beverage and food products. Net sales for
the three months
ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 were $184.2&nbsp;million, compared to 
$157.1&nbsp;million for the three months ended June
30, 2009, an increase of $27.1&nbsp;million, or 17.3%. This increase was 
primarily
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->43<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">due to an increase in
the sales price of gasoline and diesel fuel. The average sales price per gallon 
including
excise taxes increased from $2.32 in the second quarter of 2009, to $2.82 in the
second quarter of
2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Cost of Products Sold (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Cost of products sold
includes costs of gasoline and diesel fuel net of excise taxes, general 
merchandise, and beverage
and food products. Cost of products sold was $158.3&nbsp;million for the three 
months ended June&nbsp;30,
2010, compared to $132.3&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009, an increase of $26.0
million, or 19.7%. This increase was primarily due to increased costs of 
gasoline and diesel fuel.
Average fuel cost per gallon including excise taxes increased from $2.14 in the 
second quarter of
2009, to $2.62 in the second quarter of 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Direct Operating Expenses (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Direct operating
expenses include costs associated with the operations of our retail division
such as labor, repairs
and maintenance, rentals and leases, insurance, property taxes, and 
environmental compliance costs.
Direct operating expenses were $16.8&nbsp;million for the three months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2010, compared to
$16.5&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase of
$0.3&nbsp;million, or 1.8%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Selling, General, and Administrative 
Expenses. </I>Selling, general, and administrative expenses
consist primarily of overhead and marketing expenses. Selling, general, and 
administrative
expenses were $1.3&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, 
compared to $1.8&nbsp;million for
the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a decrease of $0.5&nbsp;million, or 
27.8%. This decrease was
primarily due to decreased personnel costs ($0.3&nbsp;million) and decreased 
insurance expense ($0.3
million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Goodwill Impairment Loss. </I>Based on our
annual goodwill impairment test performed as of June
30, 2009, we determined that all of the goodwill in the reporting unit of our 
retail group was
impaired. The total impact of the goodwill impairment in the three months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2009 was
a non-cash charge of $27.6&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Depreciation and Amortization. 
</I>Depreciation and amortization for the three months ended June
30, 2010 was $2.7&nbsp;million, compared to $2.6&nbsp;million for the three 
months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an
increase of $0.1&nbsp;million, or 3.8%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Operating Income (Loss). </I>Operating 
income for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 was $5.1
million, compared to operating loss of $23.7&nbsp;million for the three months 
ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an
increase of $28.8&nbsp;million, or 121.5%. This increase was primarily due to a 
goodwill impairment
loss in the second quarter of 2009 and increased fuel margins in the second 
quarter of 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Six Months 
Ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 Compared to the Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009</I></B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Net Sales. </I>Net sales consist primarily
of gross sales of gasoline and diesel fuel net of
excise taxes, general merchandise, and beverage and food products. Net sales for
the six months
ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 were $342.8&nbsp;million, compared to
$289.7&nbsp;million for the six months ended June
30, 2009, an increase of $53.1&nbsp;million, or 18.3%. This increase was 
primarily due to an increase
in the sales price of gasoline and diesel fuel. The average sales price per 
gallon including
excise taxes increased from $2.15 in the second quarter of 2009, to $2.78 in the
second quarter of
2010. This increase was partially offset by decreased merchandise sales.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Cost of Products Sold (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Cost of products sold
includes costs of gasoline and diesel fuel net of excise taxes, general 
merchandise, and beverage
and food products. Cost of products sold was $296.4&nbsp;million for the six 
months ended June&nbsp;30,
2010, compared to $243.6&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009, an increase of $52.8
million, or 21.7%. This increase was primarily due to increased costs of 
gasoline and diesel fuel.
Average fuel cost per gallon including excise taxes increased from $1.99 in the 
second quarter of
2009, to $2.61 in the second quarter of 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Direct Operating Expenses (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Direct operating
expenses include costs associated with the operations of our retail division 
such as labor, repairs
and maintenance, rentals and leases, insurance, property taxes, and 
environmental compliance costs. Direct operating expenses were $33.0
million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, compared to 
$32.3&nbsp;million for the six months ended
June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase of $0.7&nbsp;million, or 2.2%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Selling, General, and Administrative 
Expenses. </I>Selling, general, and administrative expenses
consist primarily of overhead and marketing expenses. Selling, general, and 
administrative
expenses were $2.0&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, 
compared to $3.2&nbsp;million for the
six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a decrease of $1.2&nbsp;million, or 37.5%. 
This decrease was primarily
due to decreased personnel costs ($1.1&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->44<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Goodwill Impairment Loss. </I>Based on our
annual goodwill impairment test performed as of June
30, 2009, we determined that all of the goodwill in the reporting unit of our
retail group was
impaired. The total impact of the goodwill impairment in the six months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2009 was a
non-cash charge of $27.6&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Depreciation and Amortization. 
</I>Depreciation and amortization for the six months ended June
30, 2010 was $5.1&nbsp;million, compared to $4.9&nbsp;million for the six months
ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an
increase of $0.2&nbsp;million, or 4.1%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Operating Income (Loss). </I>Operating 
income for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 was $6.3
million, compared to operating loss of $21.9&nbsp;million for the six months 
ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an
increase of $28.2&nbsp;million, or 128.8%. This increase was primarily due to a 
goodwill impairment
loss in the first half of 2009.
</DIV>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD nowrap align="left">(1)</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>Fuel margin per gallon is a measurement calculated by dividing the 
difference between fuel
sales and cost of fuel sales for our wholesale segment by the number of gallons 
sold.</TD>
</TR>
<TR style="font-size: 3pt"><TD>&nbsp;</TD></TR>
<TR valign="top">
    <TD nowrap align="left">(2)</TD>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>Lubricant margin is a measurement calculated by dividing the difference
between lubricant
sales and lubricant cost of products sold by lubricant sales. Lubricant margin 
is a measure
frequently used in the petroleum products wholesale industry to measure 
operating results
related to lubricant sales.</TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Three Months 
Ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 Compared to the Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009</I></B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Net Sales. </I>Net sales consist primarily
of sales of refined products net of excise taxes,
lubricants, and freight. Net sales for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010
were $637.0&nbsp;million,
compared to $386.3&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, 
an increase of $250.7&nbsp;million,
or 64.9%. This increase was primarily due to an increase in the average sales 
price of refined
products and increased fuel sales volume. The average sales price per gallon of 
refined products,
including excise taxes, increased from $2.02 in the second quarter of 2009 to 
$2.96 in the second
quarter of 2010. Fuel sales volume increased from 198.8&nbsp;million gallons in 
the second quarter of
2009 to 224.7&nbsp;million gallons for the same period in 2010. This increase 
was partially offset by a
decrease in lubricant sales volume. Lubricant sales volume decreased from 
3.0&nbsp;million gallons in
the second quarter of 2009 to 2.7&nbsp;million gallons in the second quarter of 
2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Cost of Products Sold (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Cost of products sold
includes costs of refined products net of excise taxes, lubricants, and delivery
freight. Cost of
products sold was $615.4&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2010, compared to $365.5
million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase of 
$249.9&nbsp;million, or 68.4%. This
increase was primarily due to increased costs of refined products and purchased 
fuel volume. The
average cost per gallon of refined products, including excise taxes, increased 
from $1.95 in the
second quarter of 2009 to $2.89 in the second quarter of 2010. This increase was
partially offset
by a decrease in purchased volume of lubricant.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Direct Operating Expenses (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Direct operating
expenses include costs associated with the operations of our wholesale division 
such as labor,
repairs and maintenance, rentals and leases, insurance, property taxes, and 
environmental
compliance costs. Direct operating expenses were $12.4&nbsp;million for the 
three months ended June&nbsp;30,
2010, compared to $13.4&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009, a decrease of $1.0
million, or 7.5%. This decrease primarily resulted from lower personnel costs 
($1.7&nbsp;million).
This decrease was partially offset by increased vehicle fuel costs 
($0.5&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Selling, General, and Administrative 
Expenses. </I>Selling, general, and administrative expenses
consist primarily of overhead and marketing expenses. Selling, general, and 
administrative
expenses were $2.9&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, 
compared to $4.1&nbsp;million for
the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a decrease of $1.2&nbsp;million, or 
29.3%. This decrease
primarily resulted from lower personnel costs ($0.9&nbsp;million) and decreased 
taxes, licenses, and
fees ($0.1&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Goodwill Impairment Loss. </I>Based on the
results of our annual impairment analysis performed as
of June&nbsp;30, 2009, we determined that all of the goodwill in the reporting 
unit of our wholesale
group was impaired. The total impact of the goodwill impairment in the three 
months ended June&nbsp;30,
2009 was a non-cash charge of $41.2&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Depreciation and Amortization. 
</I>Depreciation and amortization for the three months ended June
30, 2010 was $1.3&nbsp;million, compared to $1.4&nbsp;million for the three 
months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a
decrease of $0.1&nbsp;million, or 7.1%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Operating Income. </I>Operating income for
the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 was $5.0&nbsp;million,
compared to operating loss of $39.3&nbsp;million for the three months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase
of $44.3&nbsp;million, or 112.7%. This increase was primarily due to a goodwill
impairment loss in the
three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009 and decreased direct operating expenses 
and selling, general, and
administrative expenses for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Six Months 
Ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 Compared to the Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009</I></B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Net Sales. </I>Net sales consist primarily
of sales of refined products net of excise taxes,
lubricants, and freight. Net sales for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 
were $1,150.9&nbsp;million,
compared to $717.3&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an 
increase of $433.6&nbsp;million,
or 60.4%. This increase was primarily due to an increase in the average sales 
price of refined
products and increased fuel sales volume. The average sales price per gallon of 
refined products,
including excise taxes, increased from $1.89 in the first half of 2009 to $2.80 
in the first half
of 2010. Fuel sales volume increased from 397.9&nbsp;million gallons in the 
first half of 2009 to 431.8
million gallons for the same period in 2010. This increase was partially offset 
by a decrease in
the average price of lubricants and sales volume. The lubricant average price 
per gallon decreased
from $9.86 in the first half of 2009 to $9.46 in the first half of 2010. 
Lubricant sales volume
decreased from 6.1&nbsp;million gallons for the first half of 2009 to 
5.2&nbsp;million for the same period in
2010.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->46<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Cost of Products Sold (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Cost of products
sold includes costs of refined products net of excise taxes, lubricants, and 
delivery freight.
Cost of products sold was $1,109.3&nbsp;million for the six months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2010, compared to
$675.2&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase of 
$434.1&nbsp;million, or 64.3%.
This increase was primarily due to increased costs of refined products and 
purchased fuel volume.
The average cost per gallon of refined products, including excise taxes,
increased from $1.82 in
the first half of 2009 to $2.73 in the first half of 2010. This increase was 
partially offset by a
decrease in the average cost of lubricants and purchased volume. The lubricant 
average cost per
gallon decreased from $9.03 in the first half of 2009 to $8.38 in the first half
of 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Direct Operating Expenses (exclusive of 
depreciation and amortization). </I>Direct operating
expenses include costs associated with the operations of our wholesale division 
such as labor,
repairs and maintenance, rentals and leases, insurance, property taxes, and 
environmental
compliance costs. Direct operating expenses were $22.4&nbsp;million for the six 
months ended June&nbsp;30,
2010, compared to $27.4&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009, a decrease of $5.0&nbsp;million,
or 18.2%. This decrease primarily resulted from lower personnel costs 
($5.9&nbsp;million). This
decrease was partially offset by increased vehicle fuel costs 
($0.9&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Selling, General, and Administrative 
Expenses. </I>Selling, general, and administrative expenses
consist primarily of overhead and marketing expenses. Selling, general, and 
administrative
expenses were $4.9&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, 
compared to $8.9&nbsp;million for the
six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a decrease of $4.0&nbsp;million, or 44.9%. 
This decrease primarily
resulted from lower personnel costs ($3.1&nbsp;million) and decreased bad debt 
expense ($0.6&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Goodwill Impairment Loss. </I>Based on the
results of our annual impairment analysis performed as
of June&nbsp;30, 2009, we determined that all of the goodwill in the reporting 
unit of our wholesale
group was impaired. The total impact of the goodwill impairment in the six 
months ended June&nbsp;30,
2009 was a non-cash charge of $41.2&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Depreciation and Amortization. 
</I>Depreciation and amortization for the six months ended June
30, 2010 was $2.7&nbsp;million, compared to $2.8&nbsp;million for the six months
ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, a
decrease of $0.1&nbsp;million, or 3.6%.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Operating Income. </I>Operating income for
the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 was $11.6&nbsp;million,
compared to operating loss of $38.2&nbsp;million for the six months ended 
June&nbsp;30, 2009, an increase of
$49.8&nbsp;million, or 130.4%. This increase was primarily due to a goodwill 
impairment loss in the six
months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009 and decreased direct operating expenses and 
selling, general, and
administrative expenses for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>Outlook</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The impact of a continued weak economy, 
reduced demand for refined products, and narrowing
differentials between light and heavy crude oil prices negatively impacted our 
refining margins
throughout much of 2009 and the first half of 2010. New global refining capacity
has also led to
an increase in refined product inventories that has caused downward pressure on 
margins. Until the
economy recovers and demand improves, we expect refining margins to continue to 
be negatively
impacted. Also, as a result of these current unfavorable industry fundamentals, 
several refineries
in North America have been temporarily or permanently idled.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The recent financial performance of our 
Yorktown refinery has negatively impacted our overall
results of operations. Particularly, narrow heavy sour crude oil differentials 
have had a
significant impact on operating results at Yorktown. Such narrow crude oil 
differentials combined
with lower margins have made the Yorktown refinery uneconomical to operate. In 
response to these
current and anticipated near-term market conditions at Yorktown, on 
August&nbsp;3, 2010, the Board of
Directors approved the suspension of refining operations at the Yorktown 
refinery. The Yorktown
refinery will continue to be operated as a refined product distribution 
terminal. The Company
believes that excluding one-time charges of approximately
$13&nbsp;million to be incurred in the third and fourth quarters of
this year, these terminal operations will generate positive operating cash flows
and eliminate operating
losses that were occurring at the Yorktown refinery. We will continue to 
evaluate all strategic
alternatives and if the economic environment in the Yorktown market improves 
sufficiently, we will
consider restarting refining operations. Due to the effect of the current 
unfavorable economic
conditions on the refining industry, and our expectations of a continuation of 
such conditions for
the near term, we will continue to monitor both our operating assets and capital
projects for
potential asset impairments or project write-offs until conditions improve. 
Changes in market
conditions, as well as changes in assumptions used to test for recoverability 
and to determine fair
value, could result in significant impairment charges or project write-offs in 
the future, thus
affecting our earnings.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->47<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As we entered the spring 2010 driving season,
we experienced stronger refining margins in the
Southwest. Our overall refining margins improved to $9.74 per throughput barrel 
in the second
quarter of 2010 from $6.38 per throughput barrel in the first quarter of 2010. 
So far, the third
quarter refining margins continue to be good, but are expected to be lower than 
the second quarter
of 2010. Through the end of July the Gulf Coast 3:2:1 benchmark crack spread has
averaged $8.91
per barrel compared to $9.68 per barrel for the second quarter of 2010. However,
refining margins
remain volatile due to current market conditions.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition to current market conditions, 
there are other long-term factors that may decrease
the demand for refined products, as well as increase the cost to produce refined
products. These
factors include the increased mileage standards for vehicles, the mandated 
renewable fuel
standards, proposed climate change legislation, regulation of greenhouse gas 
emissions under the
Clean Air Act, and competing refineries overseas.
</DIV>
<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>Liquidity and 
Capital Resources</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our primary sources of liquidity are cash 
generated from our operating activities, existing
cash balances, and our revolving credit facility. Our ability to generate 
sufficient cash flows
from our operating activities will continue to be primarily dependent on 
producing or purchasing,
and selling, sufficient quantities of refined products at margins sufficient to 
cover fixed and
variable expenses. The modestly improving refining margin environment during the
first half of
2010, compared to the fourth quarter of 2009, positively impacted our earnings 
and cash flows. Our
refining gross margin increased from $4.89 per throughput barrel in the fourth 
quarter of 2009 to
$6.38 per throughput barrel in the first quarter of 2010, and to $9.74 per 
throughput barrel in
the second quarter of 2010. However, a planned 19-day maintenance turnaround at 
our El Paso
refinery and a planned 10-day outage at our Gallup refinery during the first 
quarter of 2010
resulted in a temporary increase in inventory levels and prepaid inventory
purchases compared to
the fourth quarter of 2009.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Refining margins may be volatile in 
subsequent quarters. Our margins may deteriorate
significantly, potentially reducing our earnings and cash flows. In addition, 
our future capital
expenditures and other cash requirements could be higher than we currently 
expect as a result of
various factors described in Part&nbsp;I, Item&nbsp;1A &#147;Risk Factors&#148; 
in our 2009 annual report on Form 10-K
and elsewhere in this quarterly report. If any of these events should transpire,
we could be
unable to comply with the financial covenants set forth in our credit facilities
(described below).
If we fail to achieve the financial covenant threshold levels, we could be 
prohibited from
borrowing under our revolving credit facility for our working capital needs or 
issuing letters of
credit, which would hinder our ability to purchase sufficient quantities of 
crude oil to operate
our refineries at planned rates. To the extent that we are unable to generate 
sufficient cash
flows from operations, or if we are unable to borrow or issue letters of credit 
under the revolving
credit facility, we would need to seek additional financing, if available, in 
order to operate our
business.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We are considering additional alternatives to
further improve our capital structure by
increasing our cash balances and/or reducing or refinancing a portion of the 
remaining balance on
our Term Loan. These alternatives include various strategic initiatives and 
potential asset sales
as well as potential public or private equity or debt financings. If additional 
funds are obtained
by issuing equity securities, our existing stockholders could be diluted. We can
give no
assurances that we will be able to sell any of our assets or obtain additional 
financing on terms
acceptable to us, or at all. However, given our view of current operations, our 
outlook on
refining margins and the overall economy and the credit and capital markets, we 
anticipate that we
will be able to satisfy our working capital requirements in the near term.
</DIV>

million compared to net cash generated for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2009 of $120.5&nbsp;million.
The most significant providers of cash during the first six months of 2010 were 
adjustments to net
income for non-cash items such as depreciation and amortization 
($69.0&nbsp;million), amortization of
original issue discount ($7.7&nbsp;million), amortization of loan fees 
($4.8&nbsp;million), and stock-based
compensation ($2.5&nbsp;million). The most significant uses of cash were net 
cash outflows from a
temporary investment in inventory levels ($25.7&nbsp;million), prepaid inventory
purchases primarily for
the procurement of crude oil ($123.1&nbsp;million), and accounts payable 
($55.1&nbsp;million).

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net cash provided by operating activities for
the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009 was $120.5
million. The most significant providers of cash were adjustments to net income 
for non-cash items
such as goodwill impairment loss ($299.6&nbsp;million), depreciation and 
amortization ($74.7&nbsp;million),
write-off of unamortized loan fees ($9.0&nbsp;million), deferred income taxes 
($42.6&nbsp;million),
amortization of loan fees ($3.7&nbsp;million), and stock-based compensation 
($2.3&nbsp;million). These
increases in cash were partially offset by a net cash outflow from an increase 
in accounts
receivable ($60.9&nbsp;million), prepaid expenses ($31.8&nbsp;million), and an 
increase in other accrued
liabilities ($24.6&nbsp;million) offset by cash generated by accounts payable 
($75.0&nbsp;million).

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Indebtedness</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Senior Secured Notes. </I>In 
June&nbsp;2009, we issued two tranches of Senior Secured Notes under an
indenture dated June&nbsp;12, 2009. The first tranche consisted of 
$325.0&nbsp;million in aggregate
principal amount of 11.25% Senior Secured Notes, or the Fixed Rate Notes. The 
second tranche
consisted of $275.0&nbsp;million Senior Secured Floating Rate Notes, or the 
Floating Rate Notes, and
together with the Fixed Rate Notes, the Senior Secured Notes. The Fixed Rate 
Notes mature on June
15, 2017 and pay interest semi-annually in arrears on June&nbsp;15 and 
December&nbsp;15 of each year,
beginning on December&nbsp;15, 2009 at a rate of 11.25% per annum. The Fixed 
Rate Notes may be redeemed
by us at our option beginning on June&nbsp;15, 2013 through June&nbsp;14, 2014 
at a premium of 5.625%; from
June&nbsp;15, 2014 through June&nbsp;14, 2015 at a premium of 2.813%; and at par
thereafter. As of June&nbsp;30,
2010, the fair value of the Fixed Rate Notes was $290.9&nbsp;million. The 
Floating Rate Notes mature on
June&nbsp;15, 2014 and pay interest quarterly beginning on September&nbsp;15, 
2009 at a per annum rate, reset
quarterly, equal to 3-month LIBOR (subject to a LIBOR floor of 3.25%) plus 
7.50%. The interest
rate on the Floating Rate Notes as of June&nbsp;30, 2010 was 10.75%. The 
Floating Rate Notes may be
redeemed by us at our option beginning on December&nbsp;15, 2011 through 
June&nbsp;14, 2012 at a premium of
5.0%; from June&nbsp;15, 2012 through June&nbsp;14, 2013 at a premium of 3.0%; 
and at a premium of 1.0%
thereafter.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top:
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Proceeds from the issuance of the Fixed Rate 
Notes were $290.7&nbsp;million, net of an original
issue discount of $27.8&nbsp;million and underwriting discounts of 
$6.5&nbsp;million. Proceeds from the
issuance of the Floating Rate Notes were $247.5&nbsp;million, net of an original
issue discount of $22.0
million and underwriting discounts of $5.5&nbsp;million. We paid 
$2.1&nbsp;million in other financing costs
related to the Senior Secured Notes. The fair value of the Floating Rate Notes 
was $247.5&nbsp;million
at June&nbsp;30, 2010. We are amortizing the original issue discounts using the 
effective interest
method over the life of the notes. The combined proceeds from the issuance and 
sale of the Senior
Secured Notes were used to repay a portion of the outstanding indebtedness under
the Term Loan
Credit Agreement, or Term Loan.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Senior Secured Notes are guaranteed by 
all of our domestic restricted subsidiaries in
existence on the date the Senior Secured Notes were issued. The Senior Secured 
Notes will also be
guaranteed by all future wholly-owned domestic restricted subsidiaries and by 
any restricted
subsidiary that guarantees any of our indebtedness under credit facilities that 
are secured by a
lien on the collateral securing the Senior Secured Notes. The Senior Secured 
Notes are also
secured on a first-priority basis, equally and ratably with our Term Loan and 
any future other pari
passu secured obligation, by the collateral securing the Term Loan, which 
consists of our fixed
assets, including our refineries, and on a second-priority basis, equally and 
ratably with the Term
Loan and any future other pari passu secured obligation, by the collateral 
securing the 2007
Revolving Credit Agreement, which consists of our cash and cash equivalents, 
trade accounts
receivable, and inventory.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The indenture governing the Senior Secured 
Notes contains covenants that limit our (and most
of our subsidiaries&#146;) ability to, among other things: (i)&nbsp;pay 
dividends or make other
distributions in respect of our capital stock or make other restricted payments;
(ii)&nbsp;make certain
investments; (iii)&nbsp;sell certain assets; (iv)&nbsp;incur additional debt or 
issue certain preferred
shares; (v)&nbsp;create liens on certain assets to secure debt; 
(vi)&nbsp;consolidate, merge, sell, or
otherwise dispose of all or substantially all of our assets; (vii)&nbsp;restrict
dividends or other
payments from restricted subsidiaries; and (viii)&nbsp;enter into certain 
transactions with our
affiliates. These covenants are subject to a number of important limitations and
exceptions. The
indenture governing the Senior Secured Notes also provides for events of 
default, which, if any of
them occur, would permit or require the principal, premium, if any, and interest
on all then
outstanding Senior Secured Notes to be due and payable immediately.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We may issue additional notes from time to 
time pursuant to the indenture governing the Senior
Secured Notes.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Convertible Senior Notes. </I>We issued 
and sold $215.5&nbsp;million in aggregate principal amount of
our 5.75% Senior Convertible Notes due 2014, or the Convertible Senior Notes, 
during June and July
2009. The Convertible Senior Notes are unsecured and pay interest semi-annually 
in arrears at a
rate of 5.75% per year beginning on December&nbsp;15, 2009. The Convertible 
Senior Notes will mature on
June&nbsp;15, 2014. The initial conversion rate for the Convertible Senior Notes
is 92.5926 shares of
common stock per $1,000 principal amount of Convertible Senior Notes (equivalent
to an initial
conversion price of approximately $10.80 per share of common stock). In lieu of 
delivery of shares
of common stock in satisfaction of our obligation upon conversion of the 
Convertible Senior Notes,
we may elect to settle conversions entirely in cash or by net share settlement. 
Proceeds from the
issuance of the Convertible Senior Notes in June and July&nbsp;2009 were 
$209.0&nbsp;million, net of
underwriting discounts of $6.5&nbsp;million, and were used to repay a portion of
outstanding
indebtedness under the Term Loan. Issuers of convertible debt instruments that 
may be settled in
cash upon conversion (including partial cash settlement) are required to 
separately account for the
liability and equity (conversion feature) components of the instruments in a 
manner reflective of
the issuer&#146;s nonconvertible debt borrowing rate. The borrowing rate used by
us to determine the
liability and equity components of the Convertible Senior Notes was 13.75%. We 
paid $0.5&nbsp;million
in other financing costs related to the Convertible Senior Notes. We valued the 
conversion feature
at $60.9&nbsp;million and recorded additional paid-in capital of 
$36.3&nbsp;million, net of deferred income
taxes of $22.6&nbsp;million and transaction costs of $2.0&nbsp;million, related 
to the equity portion
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->50<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of 
Contents</A></H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">of this convertible 
debt. The discount on the Convertible Senior Notes is amortized using the
effective interest method over the life of the notes. As of June&nbsp;30, 2010, 
the fair value of the
Convertible Senior Notes was $161.3&nbsp;million and the if-converted value is
less than its principal
amount.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Term Loan Credit Agreement</I>. The Term 
Loan has a maturity date of May&nbsp;30, 2014 and is secured
by our fixed assets, including our refineries. The Term Loan provides for 
principal payments on a
quarterly basis of $13.0&nbsp;million annually until March&nbsp;31, 2014 with 
the remaining balance due on
the maturity date. We made principal payments on the Term Loan of 
$6.5&nbsp;million in the first half
of 2010 and 2009. The average interest rates under the Term Loan for the first 
half of 2010 and
2009 were 10.75% and 8.56%, respectively. As of June&nbsp;30, 2010, the interest
rate under the Term
Loan was 10.75%. We amended the Term Loan during the second and fourth quarters 
of 2009 in
connection with the new debt offerings and in order to modify certain of the 
financial covenants.
To effect these amendments, we paid $3.4&nbsp;million in amendment fees. As a 
result of the partial
paydown of the Term Loan in June&nbsp;2009, we expensed $9.0&nbsp;million during
the second quarter to
write-off a portion of the unamortized loan fees related to the Term Loan. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2010,
the fair value of the Term Loan was $317.0&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>2007 Revolving Credit Agreement</I>. The 
2007 Revolving Credit Agreement matures on May&nbsp;31, 2012
and provides loans of up to $800&nbsp;million. The 2007 Revolving Credit 
Agreement, secured by certain
cash, accounts receivable, and inventory, can be used to refinance existing 
indebtedness of us and
our subsidiaries, to finance working capital and capital expenditures, and for 
other general
corporate purposes. The 2007 Revolving Credit Agreement is a collateral-based 
facility with total
borrowing capacity, subject to borrowing base amounts based upon eligible 
receivables and
inventory, and provides for letters of credit and swing line loans. As of 
June&nbsp;30, 2010, the gross
availability under the 2007 Revolving Credit Agreement was $639.1&nbsp;million 
determined based on an
advance rate formula tied to our accounts receivable and inventory levels. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2010, we
had net availability under the 2007 Revolving Credit Agreement of 
$191.1&nbsp;million due to $263.0
million in letters of credit outstanding and $185.0&nbsp;million in outstanding 
direct borrowings. Our
average net availability under the 2007 Revolving Credit Agreement for the month
of July&nbsp;2010 was
$198.0&nbsp;million. The average interest rates under the 2007 Revolving Credit 
Agreement for the first
six months of 2010 and 2009 were 6.30% and 5.50%, respectively. At June&nbsp;30,
2010, the interest
rate under the 2007 Revolving Credit Agreement was 6.20%. We amended the 2007 
Revolving Credit
Agreement during the second and fourth quarters of 2009 in connection with the 
new debt offerings
and to modify certain of the financial covenants. We incurred $5.6&nbsp;million 
in fees related to
these amendments.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Guarantees of the Term Loan and the 
Revolving Credit Agreement. </I>The Term Loan and the 2007
Revolving Credit Agreement, or together the Agreements, are guaranteed on a 
joint and several basis
by subsidiaries of Western Refining, Inc. The guarantees related to the 
Agreements remain in
effect until such time that the terms of the Agreements are satisfied and 
subsequently terminated.
Amounts potentially due under these guarantees are equal to the amounts due and 
payable under the
respective Agreements at any given time. No amounts have been recorded for these
guarantees. The
guarantees are not subject to recourse to third parties.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Certain Covenants in Agreements. </I>The 
Agreements contain certain covenants, including
limitations on debt, investments, and dividends; and financial covenants 
relating to minimum
interest coverage, maximum leverage, and minimum EBITDA. We were in compliance 
with all applicable
covenants set forth in the Agreements at June&nbsp;30, 2010. The following table
sets forth the more
significant financial covenants on minimum consolidated EBITDA, minimum 
consolidated interest
coverage (as defined therein), and maximum consolidated leverage (as defined 
therein) by quarter:
</DIV>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top:

on a long-term purchase
contract that resulted in an annual contractual obligation of $381.5 million for
2010
and $416.9 million annually thereafter through December 31, 2019.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Off-Balance Sheet
Arrangements</B>
</DIV>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left">
<A name="109"></A>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Item&nbsp;3.
Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosure About Market Risk</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Changes in commodity prices and interest 
rates are our primary sources of market risk.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Commodity Price 
Risk</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We are exposed to market risks related to the
volatility of crude oil and refined product
prices, as well as volatility in the price of natural gas used in our refinery 
operations. Our
financial results can be affected significantly by fluctuations in these prices,
which depend on
many factors, including demand for crude oil, gasoline and other refined 
products; changes in the
economy; worldwide production levels; worldwide inventory levels; and 
governmental regulatory
initiatives. Our risk management strategy identifies circumstances in which we 
may utilize the
commodity futures market to manage risk associated with these price 
fluctuations.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In order to manage the uncertainty relating 
to inventory price volatility, we have generally
applied a policy of maintaining inventories at or below a targeted operating 
level. In the past,
circumstances have occurred, such as turnaround schedules or shifts in market 
demand that have
resulted in variances between our actual inventory level and our desired target 
level. We may
utilize the commodity futures market to manage these anticipated inventory 
variances.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We maintain inventories of crude oil, other 
feedstocks and blendstocks, and refined products,
the values of which are subject to wide fluctuations in market prices driven by 
worldwide economic
conditions, regional and global inventory levels, and seasonal conditions. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2010, we
held approximately 6.7&nbsp;million barrels of crude oil, refined product, and 
other inventories valued
under the LIFO valuation method with an average cost of $57.48 per barrel. At 
June&nbsp;30, 2010, the
excess of the current cost of our crude oil, refined products, and other 
feedstocks and blendstocks
inventories over aggregated LIFO costs was $123.5&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In accordance with FASC 161, <I>Accounting 
for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities, </I>all
commodity futures contracts, price swaps, and options are recorded at fair value
and any changes in
fair value between periods are recorded in our Condensed Consolidated Statements
of Operations as a
component of cost of products sold.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We selectively utilize commodity derivatives 
to manage our price exposure to inventory
positions or to fix margins on certain future sales volumes. The commodity 
derivative instruments
may take the form of futures contracts, price swaps, or options and are entered 
into with
counterparties that we believe to be creditworthy. We elected not to pursue 
hedge accounting
treatment for these instruments for financial accounting purposes. Therefore, 
changes in the fair
value of these derivative instruments are included in income in the period of 
change. Net gains or
losses associated with these transactions are reflected in cost of products sold
at the end of each
period. For the three and six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2010, we had 
$0.3&nbsp;million and $3.2&nbsp;million,
respectively, in net losses settled or accounted for using mark-to-market 
accounting. For the
three and six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2009, we had $11.3&nbsp;million and 
$12.5&nbsp;million, respectively, in
net realized and unrealized losses accounted for using mark-to-market 
accounting.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At June&nbsp;30, 2010, we had open commodity 
derivative instruments consisting of crude oil futures
and finished product price swaps on a net 548,000 barrels to protect the value 
of certain crude
oil, finished product, and blendstock inventories for future quarters in 2010. 
These open
instruments had total unrealized net gains at June&nbsp;30, 2010, of 
$1.3&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 
2010, we did not have any commodity derivative
instruments that were designated and accounted for as hedges.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Interest Rate 
Risk</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of June&nbsp;30, 2010, $808.3&nbsp;million
of our outstanding debt, excluding unamortized discount,
was at floating interest rates based on LIBOR and prime rates. An increase in 
these base rates of
1% would increase our interest expense by $8.1&nbsp;million per year.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->52<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

Controls and Procedures</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company, under the supervision and with 
the participation of its management, including the
Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, has evaluated the 
effectiveness of the
Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures, as defined in Rules&nbsp;13a-
15(e) and 15d-15(e) of the
Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as of June&nbsp;30, 2010. Based on that 
evaluation, the Company&#146;s
Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer concluded that the 
Company&#146;s disclosure
controls and procedures were effective as of June&nbsp;30, 2010.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 
6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There were no changes in the Company&#146;s 
internal control over financial reporting during the
quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2010 that have materially affected, or are 
reasonably likely to
materially affect, the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting.

are subject to periodic lawsuits, investigations
and claims, including environmental claims and employee-related matters. We 
incorporate by
reference the information regarding contingencies in Note 22, 
&#147;Contingencies,&#148; to our Condensed
Consolidated Financial Statements set forth in <I>Item&nbsp;8. Financial 
Statements and Supplementary Data</I>
of our 2009 annual report on Form 10-K. In addition, we incorporate by reference
the Legal Matters
section of Note 19, &#147;Contingencies,&#148; from this Form 10-Q. Other than 
as described in Note 19,
there were no material developments during the quarter in any of the legal 
proceedings described
therein. Although we cannot predict with certainty the ultimate resolution of 
lawsuits,
investigations and claims asserted against us, we do not believe that any 
currently pending legal
proceeding or proceedings to which we are a party will have a material adverse 
effect on our
business, financial condition, or results of operations.
